## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, where stress depends on strain through elastic/plastic deformation mechanisms and on temperature through thermal softening or thermally-activated processes.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity with constant modulus)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear modulus variation with temperature)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic strain hardening)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + epsilon)**c2 (elastic-plastic transition)
- Johnson-Cook strength term: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) (strain hardening with yield stress)
- Johnson-Cook with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T**c5) (combined hardening and softening)
- Arrhenius thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (thermally activated softening with hardening)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon))) * (c3 + c4 * T) (saturation hardening with thermal effect)
- Polynomial in strain with thermal factor: sigma = (c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2) * (c2 + c3 * T) (nonlinear elasticity with temperature)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Thermal softening rational form: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * c2 / (c3 + T) (inverse temperature dependence)
- Hyperbolic sine flow stress: sigma = c0 * T * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 / T)) (Zener-Hollomon type creep/flow)
- Combined elastic-plastic with exponential softening: sigma = (c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (general thermomechanical model)
- Swift hardening with temperature: sigma = c0 * (c1 + epsilon)**c2 * (c3 + c4 * T) (shifted power law with thermal factor)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening at high temperatures → multiplicative factor that decreases with T, such as (1 - c*T**n), exp(-c*T), or c/(T+c1)
- Strain hardening saturation → Voce-type terms (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) indicating stress approaches a limit at large strains
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 in stress-strain relation representing initial yield before hardening
- Thermally activated processes → Arrhenius-type exp(c/T) or sinh-based terms reflecting Boltzmann statistics of dislocation motion
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → Piecewise or smooth blending between linear (c*epsilon) and power-law (epsilon**n) regimes
- Strain rate equivalence through temperature → T and strain often appear in combined Zener-Hollomon parameter exp(c/T)*epsilon_dot
- Modulus degradation → The coefficient of the linear strain term decreases with temperature, reflecting elastic softening
- Separable structure → Stress often factors as sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), with strain and temperature effects multiplicatively separable
